# Kerf ÔÇö Roadmap

**Status glyphs:** `Ôťů shipped` ┬Ě `­čÜž in flight` ┬Ě `­čö┤ not started`

---

## North Star

**The most comprehensive CAD on Earth ÔÇö a single tool in which a person can design *anything*.** Mechanical engineering, electronics, PCB, architecture, civil engineering, drafting, jewelry, automotive ÔÇö and every other CAD sector, including the small and niche ones. We are doing **everything**. Nothing here is "cut." Lower priority means *later*, not *dropped*.

This is a **priority-ordered** roadmap, not a date-ordered or effort-ordered one. The tiers (P0 Ôćĺ P3) express sequence and leverage: which items earn the most credibility per unit of work.

Kerf is dual-licensed: the OSS core (MIT) and the hosted-tier code under `packages/kerf-{billing,cloud}/` + `src/cloud/`.

### Why chat-driven CAD works

Kerf is **chat-driven** CAD. Every capability is designed around one constraint:

> *Can the LLM produce and re-edit this deliverable through a text-native tool, and verify the result?*

Professional CAD is overcomplicated mostly because of command-discovery affordances (ribbons, palettes, wizards) that an LLM does not need. Kerf ships professional **capability** while deliberately not shipping professional **UI complexity**. This makes the roadmap shorter than it looks: many "pro features" are UX wrappers around a parametric core we expose as a text schema + LLM tool + verifier.

**Hard guardrail:** simplification is about *authoring mechanics only*. It is never an excuse to drop a domain or to skimp on correctness, output formats, or standards compliance. Those are *more* important under an LLM, not less.

---

## Platform foundation

The sector work only matters if you **own your work, are not locked in, and can run Kerf wherever you want**. Four commitments, all decided:

1. **Every cloud project is a real git repository** ÔÇö `git clone`-able with stock git, no special client. Large or binary files are auto-detected and stored with a small in-git pointer. Version control is two complementary layers: fine-grained automatic file history *and* deliberate, shareable commits with GitHub sync.

2. **One client, cloud by default, easy optional self-host** ÔÇö `pip install kerf` for the hosted cloud; `pip install 'kerf[server]'` + bring-your-own-Postgres + `kerf serve` for self-host. Same client, same data model, both paths first-class.

3. **Portability is the anti-lock-in guarantee** ÔÇö `kerf sync` mirrors to a local folder with two-way sync; `kerf export` / `kerf import` produce and ingest a plain file tree. Moving a project between cloud and self-host is painless.

4. **A fully-local / offline desktop app is committed but demand-gated** ÔÇö portability + two-way sync + easy self-host is the complete launch answer to "I want to own my data." The standalone offline desktop build is sequenced behind real demand.

---

## What shipped

### Latest delta ÔÇö 2026-05-31

**ELEC-OPTOCOUPLER-CTR** Ôťů ÔÇö Optocoupler isolation circuit analysis: given LED forward current IF, CTR(min/typ/max), output pull-up R_L, supply Vcc, and load capacitance C_L, computes IC (min/typ/max), saturation threshold IC_sat = Vcc/R_L, saturation verdict, Vout_low = Vce_sat, Vout_high = Vcc, output rise/fall time, and headroom factor. `analyze_optocoupler(OptocouplerSpec, CircuitSpec) -> OptocouplerReport` in `kerf_electronics.optocoupler_ctr`. Dataclasses: `OptocouplerSpec` (model, IF_mA, CTR_min_percent, CTR_typ_percent, CTR_max_percent, Vce_sat_V, IF_max_mA, Vf_typ_V=1.2, t_rise_us_at_Rl=(2.0, 1000)); `CircuitSpec` (Vcc_out_V, R_pullup_ohm, C_load_pF=20.0, R_LED_series_ohm, V_LED_drive_V); `OptocouplerReport` (IC_min_mA, IC_typ_mA, IC_max_mA, IC_saturation_mA, saturated_min_case, Vout_low_V, Vout_high_V, t_rise_us, t_fall_us, headroom_factor_min, warnings, honest_caveat). Algorithm: IC = CTR/100 ├Ś IF_mA (IEC 60747-5-5 ┬ž6.3); IC_sat = Vcc/R_L ├Ś 1000 [mA]; saturated_min_case = (IC_min >= IC_sat); headroom = IC_min/IC_sat; t_rise = max(2.2├ŚR_L├ŚC_L, t_rise_spec├ŚR_L_actual/R_L_spec) [┬Ás]; t_fall = t_rise (symmetric R-C model). Warns: IF > IF_max (over-drive); NOT saturated (IC_min < IC_sat, suggests fix); headroom < 2.0 (aging margin); IF mismatch (circuit-derived IF vs spec IF > 25%). `elec_analyze_optocoupler` LLM tool registered in plugin.py; re-exported from `kerf_electronics/__init__.py`. 68 tests green. HONEST: LINEAR CTR MODEL ONLY ÔÇö IC = CTR/100 ├Ś IF; real CTR vs IF is non-linear (peaks at moderate IF, falls at extremes); TEMPERATURE AND LIFETIME DERATING NOT MODELLED ÔÇö CTR degrades 30ÔÇô50% over LED lifetime at elevated temperature (Avago AN-5078 ┬ž4.3); always derate CTR to the datasheet minimum at maximum rated temperature (NOT the 25┬░C value); Vce_sat is a fixed datasheet spec (actual depends on IC + temperature); rise/fall time is an RC estimate (2.2├ŚR_L├ŚC_L) ÔÇö minority-carrier storage NOT modelled; for high-speed designs use t_PLH/t_PHL from the datasheet at exact R_L and V_CC; isolation voltage (V_IORM, IEC 60747-5-5 creepage/clearance) NOT checked. Refs: Vishay Application Note AN-38 "Optocoupler Output Response Time"; Avago/Broadcom Application Note 5078 "Using Optocouplers"; IEC 60747-5-5:2007 ┬ž6.3 ÔÇö `packages/kerf-electronics/src/kerf_electronics/optocoupler_ctr.py`.

**ELEC-ZENER-TC-DRIFT** Ôťů ÔÇö Zener voltage drift over temperature using temperature coefficient TC (mV/┬░C). Models the Vz vs T curve which has a zero-TC crossing near 5.6 V (above: positive TC dominated by avalanche; below: negative TC dominated by Zener tunneling). `compute_zener_drift(ZenerSpec, OperatingSpec) -> ZenerDriftReport` in `kerf_electronics.zener_tc_drift`. Dataclasses: `ZenerSpec` (Vz_nominal_V, TC_mV_per_C, test_current_mA, test_temp_C=25.0); `OperatingSpec` (current_mA, ambient_temp_C_min, ambient_temp_C_max); `ZenerDriftReport` (Vz_at_min_temp_V, Vz_at_max_temp_V, Vz_drift_total_V, Vz_drift_percent, current_dependence_warning, recommendation, honest_caveat). Algorithm: rZÔëł0.01├ŚVz/Iz_test [╬ę] (Vishay AN-2014-3 ┬ž2.2); ╬öVz_current=rZ├Ś(Iz_opÔłĺIz_test) [V]; Vz(T)=(Vz_nom+╬öVz_current)+TC├Ś10Ôü╗┬│├Ś(TÔłĺT_test) [V]; drift_percent=100├Ś|Vz(T_max)ÔłĺVz(T_min)|/Vz_nom; current deviation >50% triggers warning. Recommendation: drift>5% Ôćĺ suggest 5.6V near-zero-TC Zener (BZX55C5V6, 1N5232B) or bandgap Vref IC (LM4040, ADR4550, LT6656). Physical basis: Zener tunneling (Vz<5V, negative TC, band-gap narrowing ÔłéEg/ÔłéT<0 per Varshni equation); avalanche impact ionisation (Vz>7V, positive TC, phonon scattering reduces carrier mean free path); mixed regime 5ÔÇô7V with TCÔëł0 near 5.6V (device-process-specific). `elec_compute_zener_drift` LLM tool registered in plugin.py; re-exported from `kerf_electronics/__init__.py`. 24 tests green. HONEST: LINEAR TC MODEL ONLY ÔÇö real Vz vs T is mildly quadratic in the 5ÔÇô7V transition region (second-order deviation ┬▒0.1ÔÇô0.3 mV / 100┬░C, Sze ┬ž4.5 Fig. 4.5-6); TC is current-dependent (┬▒10ÔÇô20% at significantly different Iz); part-to-part TC spread ┬▒30ÔÇô50% for C-suffix Zeners; thermal self-heating NOT modelled (T_j=T_amb+╬ŞJA├ŚP_Z, ╬ŞJA~300ÔÇô600┬░C/W for DO-35/SOD-80); rZ linearisation valid only within ~50% of Iz_test; zero-TC crossing is device/manufacturer-specific. Refs: S. M. Sze "Physics of Semiconductor Devices" 3e ┬ž4.5; H&H ┬ž2.2.4 Table 2.1; Vishay AN-2014-3 ┬ž2.4; ON AN-961 ┬ž3 ÔÇö `packages/kerf-electronics/src/kerf_electronics/zener_tc_drift.py`.

**ELEC-ZENER-CLAMP** Ôťů ÔÇö Zener-diode voltage clamp + series resistor design for DC supply rail regulation. `design_zener_clamp(ZenerClampSpec) -> ZenerClampReport` in `kerf_electronics.zener_clamp_design`. Dataclasses: `ZenerClampSpec` (V_in_min_V, V_in_max_V, V_zener_V, I_load_min_A, I_load_max_A, V_zener_tolerance_pct=5.0, I_zener_knee_A=0.001); `ZenerClampReport` (R_series_ohm, R_series_power_W, I_zener_max_A, P_zener_max_W, recommended_zener_package, recommended_R_E12_ohm, regulation_pct, honest_caveat). Algorithm: R = (V_in_max Ôłĺ V_Z) / (I_load_min + I_knee); V_Z_max = V_Z├Ś(1+tol/100); I_Z_max = (V_in_max Ôłĺ V_Z_max)/R Ôłĺ I_load_min; P_Z_design = V_Z ├Ś I_Z_max ├Ś 1.25 (25% derating margin per Vishay AN-2014-3 ┬ž3); P_R = (V_in_max Ôłĺ V_Z) ├Ś (I_Z_max + I_load_min). Zener package thresholds: 0.4 W (DO-35/SOD-80, BZX55 series), 0.5 W (DO-41, BZX79), 1 W (DO-41/BZX85, 1N4728ÔÇô1N4764), 3 W (DO-201/P600), 5 W (SOT-89/TO-252). E12 series resistor from IEC 60063 (round up for conservative power). `electronics_design_zener_clamp` LLM tool registered in plugin.py; re-exported from `kerf_electronics/__init__.py`. 60 tests green. HONEST: SIMPLE LINEAR SHUNT REGULATOR ONLY ÔÇö wasted power = (V_in_maxÔłĺV_Z)├ŚI_R_total regardless of load draw; at zero load ALL current flows through Zener; for I_load > 100 mA or efficiency-sensitive rails STRONGLY prefer LDO linear regulator (LM1117, MCP1700) or switching buck converter; Zener incremental resistance rZ NOT modelled (╬öV_out = rZ├Ś╬öI_Z ÔÇö typical rZ 7ÔÇô20 ╬ę for 5 V / 400 mW parts ÔÇö use TL431 or shunt reference IC for tight regulation); temperature coefficient of V_Z NOT modelled (below ~5 V TC is negative, above ~5.6 V positive; Ôëł5.1 V Zeners have ~0 TC); 25% margin is steady-state ÔÇö pulse/transient peaks require JEDEC JESD51-2 transient thermal impedance analysis; static regulation = 2├Śtol% only (dynamic line/load from rZ excluded). Refs: Horowitz & Hill "Art of Electronics" 3e ┬ž2.2.4; Vishay Application Note AN-2014-3 ÔÇö `packages/kerf-electronics/src/kerf_electronics/zener_clamp_design.py`.

**ELEC-OP-AMP-OFFSET-DRIFT** Ôťů ÔÇö Op-amp input offset voltage and temperature drift calculator for precision instrumentation design. `compute_op_amp_drift(OpAmpSpec, CircuitSpec, error_budget_pct=0.1) -> OpAmpOffsetReport` in `kerf_electronics.op_amp_offset_drift`. Dataclasses: `OpAmpSpec` (Vos_typ_uV, Vos_drift_uV_per_C, T_ambient_min_C, T_ambient_max_C, T_reference_C=25.0); `CircuitSpec` (gain_VV, signal_full_scale_V); `OpAmpOffsetReport` (Vos_at_T_min_uV, Vos_at_T_max_uV, Vos_max_input_referred_uV, Vos_max_output_referred_mV, error_pct_of_FS, within_spec, recommended_op_amp_class, honest_caveat). Algorithm: Vos(T) = Vos_typ + TC_Vos ├Ś (T Ôłĺ T_ref) (TI SLOA069 ┬ž3 Eq. 3-1); worst-case evaluates all 4 (┬▒drift ├Ś ┬▒endpoint) combinations and takes max absolute; Vos_max_IR = max(|Vos(T_min)|, |Vos(T_max)|); Vos_OR_mV = gain ├Ś Vos_max_IR / 1000; error_pct = 100 ├Ś (Vos_OR_mV/1000) / FS. Class thresholds: "chopper" (TC_Vos ÔëĄ 0.05 ┬ÁV/┬░C, e.g. AD8551, MAX420); "zero-drift" (ÔëĄ 0.1 ┬ÁV/┬░C, e.g. OPA188, LTC2050); "precision" (ÔëĄ 1.0 ┬ÁV/┬░C, e.g. OPA227, LT1012); "standard" (> 1.0 ┬ÁV/┬░C). Recommendation: "chopper" when error Ôëą 10├Ś budget; "precision" when over budget; confirm class from TC when in budget. Reference design (task spec): Vos=100 ┬ÁV, drift=2 ┬ÁV/┬░C, T=[0..70]┬░C, gain=100, FS=5V Ôćĺ Vos(T_max)=190 ┬ÁV, output=19 mV, error=0.38%. `electronics_compute_op_amp_drift` LLM tool registered in plugin.py; re-exported from `kerf_electronics/__init__.py`. 24 tests green. HONEST: linear drift model ONLY ÔÇö Vos(T)=Vos_typ+TC_Vos├Ś╬öT; real drift is non-linear and asymmetric (TI SLOA069 Fig 3-2); Vos_typ is nominal (not guaranteed ÔÇö use Vos_max for design margin); **1/f (flicker) noise contribution to DC offset NOT modelled** (can dominate sub-Hz BJT-input amps); **PSRR/CMRR cross-talk effects OUT OF SCOPE** (╬öVos_PSRR = ╬öVPS/PSRR must be added separately); resistor TC mismatch in feedback network adds gain-drift error not captured. Refs: TI "Op Amp Errors" SLOA069 ┬ž3 Eq. 3-1; Analog Devices AN-580 ┬ž1; OPA188 / AD8551 / LT1012 datasheets ÔÇö `packages/kerf-electronics/src/kerf_electronics/op_amp_offset_drift.py`.

**ELEC-INDUCTOR-CORE-SAT** Ôťů ÔÇö Inductor core saturation checker. `check_inductor_saturation(InductorCoreSpec, InductorCurrentSpec) -> CoreSaturationReport` in `kerf_electronics.inductor_core_saturation`. Dataclasses: `InductorCoreSpec` (material: "ferrite_3C95"|"ferrite_3F36"|"powdered_iron_-26"|"sendust"|"NiFe50", A_e_mm2, l_e_mm, B_sat_mT, mu_r); `InductorCurrentSpec` (turns_N, I_dc_A, I_ripple_peak_to_peak_A, temperature_C=25.0); `CoreSaturationReport` (B_peak_mT, B_sat_mT, saturation_margin_pct, saturated, recommended_max_I_dc_A, honest_caveat). Algorithm: I_pk = I_dc + I_ripple_pp/2; B_pk = ╬╝ÔéÇ┬Ě╬╝_r┬ĚN┬ĚI_pk/l_e (Ampere's law, uniform closed path); saturation_margin = (B_sat Ôłĺ B_pk)/B_sat ├Ś 100; saturated = B_pk >= B_sat; recommended_max_I_dc = max(0, 0.99┬ĚB_sat┬Ěl_e/(╬╝ÔéÇ┬Ě╬╝_r┬ĚN) Ôłĺ I_ripple/2). Temperature derating for ferrite materials: piecewise-linear (100┬░CÔćĺÔłĺ15%, 125┬░CÔćĺÔłĺ25%, 150┬░CÔćĺÔłĺ40%, 200┬░CÔćĺÔłĺ50%) per Ferroxcube 3C95/3F36 datasheets; not applied to powder-iron/Sendust/NiFe. `electronics_check_inductor_saturation` LLM tool registered in plugin.py; re-exported from `kerf_electronics/__init__.py`. 26 tests green. HONEST: fringing flux ignored (gapped cores need Dowell/Erickson ┬ž15.3 gap fringing correction); ╬╝_r assumed constant (real ferrite ╬╝_r rolls off substantially in the knee region BEFORE B_sat ÔÇö model over-estimates B_pk conservatively; use nonlinear B-H curve for precision); non-ferrite B_sat derating NOT modelled; winding I┬▓R temperature rise NOT accounted; AC core losses (Steinmetz) NOT computed ÔÇö `packages/kerf-electronics/src/kerf_electronics/inductor_core_saturation.py`. Refs: Erickson "Power Electronics" 3e ┬ž15; McLyman "Transformer and Inductor Design Handbook" 4e ┬ž10; Ferroxcube 3C95/3F36 datasheets; Magnetics Inc. Powder Core Catalog ┬ž3.

**ELEC-FET-SOA-CHECK** Ôťů ÔÇö MOSFET Safe Operating Area (SOA) checker. `check_fet_soa(FETSpec, FETOperatingPoint) -> FETSOAReport` in `kerf_electronics.fet_soa_check`. Dataclasses: `FETSpec` (part_number, V_DSS_max_V, I_D_continuous_A, I_D_pulsed_A, R_DS_on_mOhm, T_J_max_C, R_theta_JA_K_per_W, P_D_max_W); `FETOperatingPoint` (V_DS_V, I_D_A, pulse_duration_ms, duty_cycle, T_ambient_C); `FETSOAReport` (within_soa, P_diss_W, T_junction_estimate_C, soa_violation_modes, headroom_pct, honest_caveat). Algorithm: P_diss = V_DS ├Ś I_D ├Ś duty; T_J = T_amb + P_diss ├Ś R_╬ŞJA (Jedec JESD51 single-node); violation checks: V_DSS_exceeded (V_DS > V_DSS_max), I_D_continuous_exceeded (duty==1.0 AND I_D > I_D_continuous), I_D_pulsed_exceeded (duty<1.0 AND I_D > I_D_pulsed), T_J_exceeded (T_J > T_J_max), P_D_exceeded (P_diss > P_D_max); headroom_pct = (1 Ôłĺ max(utilisation_ratios)) ├Ś 100. `electronics_check_fet_soa` LLM tool registered in plugin.py; re-exported from `kerf_electronics/__init__.py`. 30 tests green. HONEST: LINEARISED SOA only ÔÇö real datasheet SOA curves (IRF Hexfet Designer's Manual ┬ž5 Fig 5-1) are non-linear in the thermal-limited and second-breakdown regions; pulse-width SOA NOT interpolated (short pulses allow higher peak I_D├ŚV_DS before the thermal integral exceeds the die's transient thermal capacity); second-breakdown (avalanche/UIS) NOT explicitly modelled as a separate boundary ÔÇö for inductive turn-off verify E_AS = ┬Ż┬ĚL┬ĚI_peak┬▓ < rated E_AS; thermal model is single-node JESD51 steady-state R_╬ŞJA (not transient Z_╬ŞJC(t)); R_DS_on is room-temperature datasheet value (actual R_DS_on increases with T_J per Infineon AN 2015-11); switching losses (turn-on, turn-off, gate charge) NOT included in P_diss ÔÇö `packages/kerf-electronics/src/kerf_electronics/fet_soa_check.py`. Refs: IRF Hexfet Designer's Manual ┬ž5; IPC-9701A; Jedec JESD51-1; Infineon AN 2015-11.

**ELEC-LDO-DROPOUT-CHECK** Ôťů ÔÇö LDO linear regulator dropout and thermal compliance checker. `check_ldo_dropout(LDOSpec) -> LDODropoutReport` in `kerf_electronics.ldo_dropout_check`. Dataclasses: `LDOSpec` (V_out_V, V_in_min_V, V_in_max_V, I_load_A, dropout_voltage_at_max_load_mV, junction_to_ambient_thermal_resistance_K_per_W, T_ambient_C=25, T_max_junction_C=125); `LDODropoutReport` (headroom_min_mV, dropout_compliant, power_dissipation_W, junction_temp_estimate_C, thermal_compliant, efficiency_pct, honest_caveat). Algorithm: headroom_mV = (V_in_min Ôłĺ V_out) ├Ś 1000; dropout_compliant = headroom_mV > dropout_spec_mV (strict); P_diss = (V_in_max Ôłĺ V_out) ├Ś I_load; T_j = T_ambient + P_diss ├Ś R_╬Şja (Jedec JESD51 single-node); thermal_compliant = T_j < T_max_junction; efficiency = 100 ├Ś V_out / V_in_max (pessimistic). `electronics_check_ldo_dropout` LLM tool registered in plugin.py; re-exported from `kerf_electronics/__init__.py`. 54 tests green. HONEST: quiescent current I_Q NOT included (dominates at light load ÔÇö TI Power Ref ┬ž3.2.3); transient headroom NOT checked (PSRR roll-off + input cap droop during load steps; add Ôëą100ÔÇô200 mV guard-band per Sandler ┬ž4.4); output capacitor stability NOT verified (ESR window requirement); thermal model is ╬Şja worst-case (╬Şjb+╬Şjc paths not modelled); efficiency = V_out/V_in_max ignores I_Q ÔÇö `packages/kerf-electronics/src/kerf_electronics/ldo_dropout_check.py`. Refs: TI Power Reference Manual ┬ž3; Sandler "Switch-Mode Power Supplies" ┬ž4; Jedec JESD51-1.

**ELEC-DC-DC-CONVERTER-RIPPLE** Ôťů ÔÇö Output voltage ripple ╬öV_out (peak-to-peak) for a buck DC-DC converter in Continuous Conduction Mode (CCM). `compute_buck_ripple(BuckConverterSpec) -> ConverterRippleReport` in `kerf_electronics.dc_dc_ripple`. Dataclasses: `BuckConverterSpec` (V_in_V, V_out_V, I_load_A, switching_freq_Hz, L_uH, C_out_uF, C_ESR_mOhm); `ConverterRippleReport` (delta_iL_pp_A, delta_V_out_pp_mV, delta_V_capacitor_mV, delta_V_ESR_mV, duty_cycle, output_ripple_pct, honest_caveat). Algorithm: D = V_out/V_in; ╬öiL = (V_inÔłĺV_out)┬ĚD/(L┬Ěf_sw); ╬öV_cap = ╬öiL/(8┬ĚC┬Ěf_sw); ╬öV_ESR = ╬öiL┬ĚESR; ╬öV_out = ╬öV_cap + ╬öV_ESR (worst-case linear sum per Erickson ┬ž2.4). CCM validity: iL_min = I_load Ôłĺ ╬öiL/2 > 0 flagged; small-ripple approximation warning when ╬öiL/(2┬ĚI_load) > 30%; ESR-dominance flag when ESR > 1/(4¤Ç┬ĚC┬Ěf_sw). `electronics_compute_buck_ripple` LLM tool registered in plugin.py; re-exported from `kerf_electronics/__init__.py`. 24 tests green. HONEST: CCM only ÔÇö DCM (iL_min < 0) NOT modelled; small-ripple approximation (Erickson ┬ž2.1) breaks above 30% load variation; D = V_out/V_in is ideal (no deadtime, body-diode drop, or min-on-pulse); ESR assumed resistive/frequency-flat (use datasheet ESR at f_sw); ╬öV_out is pessimistic linear sum (RSS is ~3ÔÇô15% less pessimistic) ÔÇö `packages/kerf-electronics/src/kerf_electronics/dc_dc_ripple.py`. Refs: Erickson "Fundamentals of Power Electronics" 3e ┬ž2.1, ┬ž2.4 Eq 2.34+2.36; Sandler "Power Electronics" ┬ž3; TI SLVA477.

**MOLD-RUNNER-DIAMETER-OPTIMIZE** Ôťů ÔÇö Optimal cold-runner diameter recommendation using the Beaumont (2007) ┬ž6.5 empirical formula D=(W^0.25├ŚÔłÜL)/3.7, balancing fill pressure against cold-runner waste. `optimize_runner_diameter(RunnerOptimizeSpec) -> RunnerOptimizeReport` in `kerf_mold.runner_diameter_optimize`. Dataclasses: `RunnerOptimizeSpec` (part_weight_g, runner_length_mm, polymer_grade, gate_count=1); `RunnerOptimizeReport` (recommended_diameter_mm, beaumont_diameter_mm, cold_runner_waste_g, fill_pressure_estimate_MPa, polymer_specific_adjustment, honest_caveat). Algorithm: D_base=(W_eff^0.25├ŚÔłÜL)/3.7 where W_eff=W/gate_count; material-viscosity adjustment: ABS+10%, PC+15% (highly viscous), PP-5% (low viscosity), PA66┬▒0%; D clamped to [1.5, 16.0] mm. Cold-runner waste = ¤Ç┬Ě(D/2)┬▓┬ĚL ├Ś ¤ü_polymer/1000 [g]; polymer densities: ABS 1.05, PC 1.20, PP 0.91, PA66 1.14 g/cm┬│ (Menges 2001 Table 2.1). Fill-pressure proxy: PÔëłK_mat┬ĚL/D^4 (Hagen-Poiseuille analogy, order-of-magnitude only). `mold_optimize_runner_diameter` LLM tool registered in plugin.py; re-exported from `kerf_mold/__init__.py`. 28 tests green. HONEST: empirical formula only ÔÇö NOT a full Hele-Shaw or Cross-WLF rheological simulation; optimises a SINGLE runner segment for one gate ÔÇö does NOT optimise filling balance in multi-cavity molds (use mold_check_runner_balance + mold_generate_runner_layout for multi-cavity networks); fill-pressure estimate is order-of-magnitude proxy only; cold-runner waste assumes cylindrical cross-section (trapezoidal/half-round runners have different volumes); confirm with Moldflow/Moldex3D/SigmaSoft fill simulation and mold trial ÔÇö `packages/kerf-mold/src/kerf_mold/runner_diameter_optimize.py`. Refs: Beaumont 2007 ┬ž6.5 (Optimal runner diameter); Menges 2001 ┬ž6.5.

**MOLD-WARPAGE-INDEX** Ôťů ÔÇö Heuristic warpage-risk index (0ÔÇô100) for injection-moulded parts. `compute_warpage_index(WarpageSpec) -> WarpageIndexReport` in `kerf_mold.warpage_index`. Dataclasses: `WarpageSpec` (wall_thickness_uniformity_pct: 0ÔÇô100, gate_location: "centered"|"edge"|"corner"|"unbalanced", polymer_grade, post_eject_cooling_time_s, mold_temp_C); `WarpageIndexReport` (warpage_index: float, risk_level: "low"|"medium"|"high"|"severe", primary_warp_driver, mitigation_suggestions: list[str], honest_caveat, sub_scores: dict). Scoring (Beaumont 2007 ┬ž10 + Menges 2001 ┬ž8): wall-uniformity penalty (0ÔÇô30 pts; piecewise linear: 100%Ôćĺ0 pts, 80%Ôćĺ6 pts, 0%Ôćĺ30 pts); gate-location penalty (0ÔÇô25 pts: centered=3, edge=14, corner=22, unbalanced=25); polymer grade (0ÔÇô20 pts: PC=5 low, ABS=7, PP=14 semi-cryst., POM=15, GF-PA66=20 max ÔÇö Menges 2001 Table 8.2 shrinkage anisotropy); post-eject cooling time (0ÔÇô15 pts; exponential decay score=15┬Ěexp(Ôłĺt/40), characteristic time 40 s per Menges 2001 ┬ž8.5 HDT stabilisation); mold temperature deviation from recommended range (0ÔÇô10 pts). Risk thresholds: 0ÔÇô24 low, 25ÔÇô49 medium, 50ÔÇô74 high, 75ÔÇô100 severe. Prioritised mitigation suggestions generated per dominant factor. `mold_compute_warpage_index` LLM tool registered in plugin.py; re-exported from `kerf_mold/__init__.py`. 39 tests green. HONEST: heuristic screening tool ONLY (┬▒15 pts uncertainty typical) ÔÇö real warpage prediction requires full filling + packing + cooling FEM simulation (Moldflow, Moldex3D, SigmaSoft 3D Warp); orientation-dependent shrinkage tensors, part geometry, packing pressure, injection speed, hold time, runner imbalance, sequential valve gating, and residual-stress relaxation are NOT modelled ÔÇö `packages/kerf-mold/src/kerf_mold/warpage_index.py`. Refs: Beaumont 2007 ┬ž10 (Warpage Analysis); Menges 2001 ┬ž8 (Post-mold shrinkage).

**MOLD-COOLING-PRESSURE-DROP** Ôťů ÔÇö Total pressure-drop across multi-segment mold cooling-channel networks (Darcy-Weisbach + minor-loss K-factors) + chiller pump head verification. `compute_cooling_pressure_drop(segments, coolant) -> CoolingPressureDropReport` in `kerf_mold.cooling_pressure_drop`. **CAM-TURNING-DEPTH** Ôťů ÔÇö Optimal depth-of-cut (DOC) per pass + total roughing passes for a lathe turning operation. `compute_turning_depth(TurningSpec) -> TurningDepthReport` in `kerf_cam.turning_depth_calc`. **GDT-FEATURE-OF-SIZE-DOF (ASME Y14.5-2018 ┬ž4.7 + ┬ž7.3)** Ôťů ÔÇö `compute_fos_dof(FOSSpec) -> FOSDoFReport` enumerates the Degrees of Freedom constrained vs released by a Feature of Size + geometric tolerance combination ÔÇö critical for inspection planning. **GDT-RUNOUT-CIRCULAR (ASME Y14.5-2018 ┬ž12.4)** Ôťů ÔÇö `check_circular_runout(CircularRunoutSpec) -> CircularRunoutReport` evaluates single-plane circular runout tolerance compliance per ┬ž12.4. Input is structured as a list of cross-section lists ÔÇö each inner list contains radial measurements at a single axial position (mirrors physical inspection: fixture at zÔéÇ, rotate 360┬░, record N radial readings). Dataclasses: `RunoutMeasurement` (angular_position_deg, radial_measurement_mm, axial_position_mm=0.0); `CircularRunoutSpec` (measurements_per_cross_section: list[list[RunoutMeasurement]], tolerance_mm, datum_axis_id="A"); `CircularRunoutReport` (fim_per_section_mm, max_fim_mm, governing_axial_position_mm, pass_fail: "PASS"|"FAIL", margin_mm, num_measurements_total, honest_caveat). Algorithm (┬ž12.4): FIM_s = max(r)Ôłĺmin(r) for each cross-section s; max_FIM = worst section; pass Ôč║ max_FIM ÔëĄ tolerance_mm. margin_mm = tolerance Ôłĺ max_FIM (positive = headroom; negative = overrun). Minimum 3 measurements per section enforced. governing_axial_position_mm identifies the worst-case section; tied FIM Ôćĺ first section wins. Distinct from runout_check.py (┬ž13 point-cloud API): section-oriented input; dedicated ┬ž12.4 compliance path; conical surface independence confirmed (per-section FIM=0 when form is perfect even though nominal radius varies axially). Oracle: eccentric cylinder eccentricity=1mm Ôćĺ FIM=2mm; tol=1mmÔćĺFAIL margin=Ôłĺ1mm; tol=2mmÔćĺPASS margin=0. `gdt_check_circular_runout` LLM tool registered via gated import; registered in plugin.py `_TOOL_MODULES`; re-exported from `kerf_cad_core.gdt`. 27 tests green. **GDT-RUNOUT-CHECK (ASME Y14.5-2018 ┬ž13 + ISO 1101:2017 ┬ž18)** Ôťů ÔÇö `check_runout(RunoutCheckSpec, list[InspectionPoint]) -> RunoutCheckReport` verifies circular and total runout tolerance compliance for a rotational feature given inspection points measured around a datum axis. Dataclasses: `InspectionPoint` (theta_deg, axial_z_mm, radius_measured_mm); `RunoutCheckSpec` (feature_id, runout_tolerance_mm, runout_type: "circular"|"total", nominal_radius_mm); `RunoutCheckReport` (max_runout_mm, mean_radius_mm, fom, compliant, per_section_runout, honest_caveat). Algorithms per ┬ž13: Circular runout (┬ž13.2 / ISO ┬ž18.3) ÔÇö group points by axial z-section, runout at each section = max(R)Ôłĺmin(R) = Full Indicator Movement (FIM); max_runout = worst section. Total runout (┬ž13.3 / ISO ┬ž18.4) ÔÇö FIM over ALL points simultaneously (max(R)Ôłĺmin(R)); captures taper/coaxiality + form combined; total_runout Ôëą circular_runout always. fom = max_runout / tolerance; fom < 1.0 Ôćĺ pass. Oracle: eccentric cylinder with 0.05 mm axis offset Ôćĺ circular runout = 2├Ś0.05 = 0.10 mm (2d formula); tapered cylinder (R=10.00Ôćĺ10.20 mm across 3 z-sections) Ôćĺ circular_runout=0 per section, total_runout=0.20 mm > circular. `gdt_check_runout` LLM tool registered via gated import pattern; registered in plugin.py `_TOOL_MODULES`; re-exported from `kerf_cad_core.gdt`. 26 tests green. HONEST FLAG: ideal datum axis assumed ÔÇö all radii must be pre-computed from a known datum axis; Chebyshev-optimal (minimum zone) axis fit (ASME B89.3.1 / ISO 12181-1 ┬ž4.3) is not performed. Circular runout grouping uses exact z-value equality ÔÇö real CMM data may require z-binning before calling. Total runout is radial-only (max RÔłĺmin R); axial deviation for face runout surfaces (ASME ┬ž13.3 full definition) is not checked ÔÇö `packages/kerf-cad-core/src/kerf_cad_core/gdt/runout_check.py`.

**GDT-DATUM-SHIFT-CHECK (ASME Y14.5-2018 ┬ž4.5 + ┬ž7.3.5)** Ôťů ÔÇö `compute_datum_shift(DatumFeatureSpec, base_position_tolerance_mm) -> DatumShiftReport` computes per-datum bonus tolerance (datum shift) when a datum feature of size is referenced with an MMC or LMC modifier in the feature control frame. **GDT-DIMENSION-CHAIN (ASME Y14.5-2018 ┬ž5.3 + Bralla ┬ž1)** Ôťů ÔÇö `compute_dimension_chain(chain: list[DimensionLink], target_gap_min_mm, target_gap_max_mm) -> DimensionChainReport` computes worst-case (WC) and statistical RSS tolerance stack-up for a linear dimension chain. Oracle: +100┬▒0.5 / Ôłĺ30┬▒0.2 / Ôłĺ20┬▒0.1 Ôćĺ nominal=50 mm; WC=[49.2, 50.8]; RSS=ÔłÜ0.30=0.5477Ôćĺ[49.452, 50.548]. `gdt_compute_dimension_chain` LLM tool registered via gated import pattern; registered in plugin.py `_TOOL_MODULES`; re-exported from `kerf_cad_core.gdt`. 24 tests green. HONEST FLAG: RSS assumes independent, normally distributed component dimensions centred on nominal (Cpk=1.0 for all links); correlation between links (e.g. same fixture datum) and non-normal distributions are not modelled ÔÇö RSS is unconservative in those cases; Monte Carlo with measured process distributions is more accurate per Bralla ┬ž1 ÔÇö `packages/kerf-cad-core/src/kerf_cad_core/gdt/dimension_chain.py`. Refs: ASME Y14.5-2018 ┬ž5.3; Bralla "Design for Manufacturability Handbook" ┬ž1.

**GK-P13 SUBD-G1-EXTRAORDINARY-PATCHES** Ôťů ÔÇö G1 continuity at extraordinary-vertex SubDÔćĺNURBS patch conversion. `convert_subd_to_g1_patches(spec: ExtraordinaryPatchSpec) -> G1PatchResult` builds n bicubic B├ęzier patches around a Catmull-Clark extraordinary vertex (valence n Ôëá 4) with Loop (1987) ┬ž4 tangent-plane continuity enforcement: (1) apply `num_iterations` CC subdivisions to isolate the EV; (2) compute EV limit position V_inf via Stam (1998) ┬ž3.1; (3) build n 4├Ś4 B├ęzier CP grids in the Stam limit-tangent plane, one per face sector; (4) project second-row CPs of adjacent patches into the Stam tangent plane at V_inf to enforce G1 across all n shared boundary edges. Dataclasses: `ExtraordinaryPatchSpec` (cage_mesh: SubdCage, extraordinary_vertex_idx: int, num_iterations: int=2); `G1PatchResult` (n_patches int = valence, patch_control_points_per_patch: list[list[list[tuple]]] 4├Ś4 CP grid per patch, max_g1_residual_deg: float, mean_g1_residual_deg: float, valence: int, honest_caveat: str). G1 residual measured as inter-patch normal angle (degrees, sampled at 5 points per shared edge). LLM tool `subd_convert_to_g1_patches` registered in plugin.py via gated import; re-exported from `kerf_cad_core.subd`. 32 oracle-asserted tests green (valence-3 cube corner 3 patches + G1 residual < 1┬░, valence-5 dome EV 5 patches + G1 < 1┬░, valence-4 regular warns + 4 patches, valence-6 hex EV 6 patches, out-of-range idx returns empty, zero iterations runs, re-export from subd package, honest_caveat mentions Loop/G1/Peters-Reif, multiple subdivision levels 1-3 finite residuals, n_patches==valence invariant). HONEST: Loop (1987) G1 construction only ÔÇö Peters-Reif G2 (curvature continuity) NOT implemented (requires degree Ôëą 5 patches, Peters-Reif 2008 ┬ž7.4); high-valence EVs (n Ôëą 8) may show curvature inflation due to convex-hull property of bicubic B├ęzier patches; G1 residual < 1┬░ achieved for n=3,5 test cases. Refs: Loop (1987) MS Thesis ┬ž4 Utah; Stam (1998) ┬ž3.1ÔÇô3.3 SIGGRAPH; Peters-Reif (2008) Subdivision Surfaces ┬ž7.4; Reif (1995) CAGD 12(2) ÔÇö `kerf-cad-core/src/kerf_cad_core/subd/g1_extraordinary_patches.py`.

**GK-P12 SUBD-STAM-LIMIT-TANGENTS** Ôťů ÔÇö exact limit tangent vectors at extraordinary Catmull-Clark SubD vertices (valence n Ôëá 4) using the eigenstructure decomposition from Stam (1998) ┬ž3.2ÔÇô3.3. `compute_stam_limit_tangents(ev: ExtraordinaryVertex, ring_positions=None) -> LimitTangentReport` computes: V_inf = w_V┬ĚV + w_e┬Ě╬úP_i + w_f┬Ě╬úQ_i (limit position, Stam ┬ž3.2 eq. 3.1); T_u = ╬ú cos(2¤Çi/n)┬Ě(P_i Ôłĺ V_inf); T_v = ╬ú sin(2¤Çi/n)┬Ě(P_i Ôłĺ V_inf) (limit tangents, Stam ┬ž3.3); N = T_u ├Ś T_v (unit normal, C┬╣-continuous at EV per Reif 1995); subdominant eigenvalue ╬╗_n = (1/4)(1 + cos(2¤Ç/n)); approximate Gaussian curvature K (angle-deficit / Gauss-Bonnet, Meyer et al. 2003 ┬ž4) and mean curvature H (cotangent-weight Laplace-Beltrami, Meyer et al. 2003 ┬ž3.3). Dataclasses: `ExtraordinaryVertex` (vertex_index, valence, position_xyz_mm, one_ring_vertices, one_ring_faces); `LimitTangentReport` (tangent_u, tangent_v, normal_xyz, gaussian_curvature_estimate, mean_curvature_estimate, valence, eigenvalue_subdominant, honest_caveat). LLM tool `subd_compute_stam_limit_tangents` registered in plugin.py via gated import; re-exported from `kerf_cad_core.subd`. 30 oracle-asserted tests green (regular v4 flat normal Z, flat T_u/T_v in XY, flat KÔëł0, flat HÔëł0, unit normal all valences, nonzero tangent magnitudes, dome v3/5/6 K>0, dome normal outward, hex v6 symmetric tangent magnitudes, eigenvalue formula for v3/4/6/5/7, limit weights partition-of-unity all n, reexport from subd package, tangents span plane, synthetic fallback no crash, honest caveat non-empty + "Stam"). DISTINCT from `limit_normal_fit.py` (which samples face grids) ÔÇö this is the closed-form Stam formula AT the extraordinary vertex point itself. HONEST: tangent vectors EXACT per Stam ┬ž3.3; curvature estimates APPROXIMATE (discrete polyhedral estimators, CC surface is only C┬╣ at EV so C┬▓-based curvature has limited meaning); distinct from the face-sampling `limit_normal_fit.py` ÔÇö `kerf-cad-core/src/kerf_cad_core/subd/stam_limit_tangents.py`. Refs: Stam (1998) ┬ž3.2ÔÇô3.3 SIGGRAPH; Reif (1995) CAGD 12(2); Catmull-Clark (1978) CAD ┬ž10(6); Meyer et al. (2003) "Discrete Differential-Geometry Operators for Triangulated 2-Manifolds" ┬ž3ÔÇô4.

**GK-P19 SUBD-FEATURE-CURVES** Ôťů ÔÇö extract characteristic "ridge" and "valley" polylines from a Catmull-Clark SubD limit surface (or refined cage) using discrete principal-curvature analysis. `extract_feature_curves(spec: FeatureCurveSpec) -> FeatureCurveResult` subdivides the cage `subdivision_level` times (Catmull-Clark 1978), estimates per-vertex normals (area-weighted face normals), computes Taubin (1995) curvature tensor at each vertex (edge normal-curvature accumulation Ôćĺ 3├Ś3 tensor projected to tangent plane Ôćĺ eigenvalues ╬║Ôéü Ôëą ╬║Ôéé), then classifies vertices as ridge (╬║Ôéü > ridge_threshold_per_mm) or valley (╬║Ôéé < Ôłĺvalley_threshold_per_mm) and chains them into polylines via BFS edge-following. Dataclasses: `FeatureCurveSpec` (cage: SubdCage, subdivision_level: int=2, ridge_threshold_per_mm: float=0.1, valley_threshold_per_mm: float=0.1); `FeatureCurve` (kind: str "ridge"|"valley", polyline_xyz_mm: list[tuple], length_mm: float, mean_principal_curvature: float); `FeatureCurveResult` (curves, num_ridges, num_valleys, total_ridge_length_mm, total_valley_length_mm, max_principal_curvature, honest_caveat). LLM tool `subd_extract_feature_curves` registered in plugin.py via gated import; re-exported from `kerf_cad_core.subd`. 26 oracle-asserted tests green (flat plane 0 ridges + 0 valleys, flat plane max ╬║Ôéü near zero, cube cage ridges detected + positive curvature + finite coords, saddle cage features detected, sphere high threshold = 0 ridges, API contracts ÔÇö empty cage, spec/dataclass defaults, kindÔłł{ridge,valley}, threshold monotonicity, re-export). Use cases: ZBrush-style topology hints; automatic UV-seam generation along high-curvature lines; feature detection for re-meshing or CAM path planning. HONEST CAVEATS: DISCRETE CURVATURE APPROXIMATION ÔÇö principal curvatures via discrete cotangent Laplacian (Meyer et al. 2003), NOT exact CC limit-surface evaluation; errors O(h┬▓) in edge length; sufficient for UV-seam/topology hints but NOT precision curvature analysis. THRESHOLD TUNING ÔÇö ridge/valley thresholds are scale-dependent (mmÔü╗┬╣); defaults (0.1 mmÔü╗┬╣) are a starting point, retune for your object scale. PERFORMANCE ÔÇö vertex count scales O(4^L) with subdivision_level L. Refs: Ohtake, Belyaev & Seidel (2004) "Ridge-Valley Lines on Meshes via Implicit Surface Fitting" SIGGRAPH; Meyer et al. (2003) "Discrete Differential-Geometry Operators for Triangulated 2-Manifolds" VisMath; Taubin (1995) "Estimating the Tensor of Curvature of a Surface" ICCV; Catmull-Clark (1978) CAD 10(6); Stam (1998) SIGGRAPH; OpenSubdiv docs ÔÇö `kerf-cad-core/src/kerf_cad_core/subd/feature_curves.py`.

**GK-P14 SUBD-CREASE-FRACTIONAL-DECAY** Ôťů ÔÇö semi-sharp fractional crease multi-level decay for Catmull-Clark SubD. `apply_fractional_crease_decay(spec: FractionalCreaseSpec) -> CreaseDecayResult` applies the DeRose-Kass-Truong (1998) ┬ž4 rule: s_new = max(0, s_old Ôłĺ 1) per subdivision level. After L levels: s_L = max(0, sÔéÇ Ôłĺ L). Dataclasses: `CreasedEdge` (v0_idx, v1_idx, sharpness Ôłł [0,Ôł×)); `FractionalCreaseSpec` (cage: SubdCage, edges: list[CreasedEdge], subdivision_level: int); `CreaseDecayResult` (decayed_edges: list[CreasedEdge], effective_dihedral_smoothing_per_edge: list[float] 0=fully sharp/1=fully smooth, max_sharpness_remaining: float, num_fully_decayed: int, honest_caveat: str). Smooth-weight formula: smooth_weight = 1 Ôłĺ clamp(s_L, 0, 1) ÔÇö matches OpenSubdiv fractional crease blend definition. Convention: s Ôëą 10 Ôëł permanently sharp (OpenSubdiv). LLM tool `subd_apply_crease_decay` registered in plugin.py via gated import; re-exported from `kerf_cad_core.subd`. 42 oracle-asserted tests green (infinite s=100 sharp at all levels, s=2 at L=0/1/2/3, s=0.5 half-sharp then smooth, mixed crease set 4 edges, monotonic increasing smooth_weight, empty edge list, level-0 identity, re-export from subd init, honest caveat non-empty + mentions schedule-only + DeRose, OpenSubdiv s=10 convention at L=9/L=10, negative sharpness clamped, large level clamps to zero, never negative). HONEST: SHARPNESS SCHEDULE ONLY ÔÇö applies the s-1 rule per level and returns decayed s-values + blend weights; does NOT simulate the resulting subdivided cage geometry, does NOT apply CC face/edge/vertex splitting operators; cage vertices/faces passed through unchanged; blended mesh evaluation (interpolating between smooth and sharp CC rules for sÔłł(0,1)) is out of scope ÔÇö `kerf-cad-core/src/kerf_cad_core/subd/crease_fractional_decay.py`. Refs: DeRose-Kass-Truong (1998) ┬ž4 SIGGRAPH; OpenSubdiv Subdivision Surfaces docs; Catmull-Clark (1978) CAD 10(6).

**SUBD-LIMIT-NORMAL-FIT** Ôťů ÔÇö sample the Catmull-Clark limit-surface normal n╠é(u,v) at a uniform (u,v) grid across all cage faces using Stam (1998) exact eigenstructure tangent vectors; `sample_subd_limit_normals(cage_mesh, samples_per_face=9, normalize=True)` returns `LimitNormalFitResult(sampled_normals, max_normal_residual_deg, mean_normal_residual_deg, num_irregular_samples, honest_caveat)`; per-face n├Śn grid (n = round(sqrt(samples_per_face))); normal via N = ÔłéS/Ôłéu ├Ś ÔłéS/Ôłév from Stam tangents (C┬╣-continuous at extraordinary vertices, exact bi-cubic B-spline for valence-4 regular faces); residuals computed against bilinear interpolation of four face-corner Stam normals ÔÇö quantifies accuracy gain of a proper normal field vs the simple shader approximation; irregular-vertex flag per sample (valence Ôëá 4 faces); LLM tool `subd_sample_limit_normals` registered in plugin via gated import; re-exported from `kerf_cad_core.subd`; 17 oracle-asserted tests (flat plane nz > 0.9999, unit-length all faces, nx/ny Ôëł 0, dot > 0.9999, normalize=True/False, result structure, total sample count, honest_caveat non-empty, irregular cube valence-3 > 0, flat plane residual < 0.5┬░, max residual ÔëĄ 90┬░, cylinder normals perpendicular to Y, cube 24-sample count + unit-length, empty cage no exception). HONEST: "fit" = residual analysis vs bilinear, NOT a closed-form NURBS surface (would require overdetermined least-squares + knot/CP storage) ÔÇö `kerf-cad-core/src/kerf_cad_core/subd/limit_normal_fit.py`. Refs: Stam (1998) ┬ž3.2; Halstead-Kass-DeRose (1993); Piegl-Tiller ┬ž9.

**ARCH-BEAM-DEFLECTION (Roark 9e ┬ž8 + AISC Manual Table 3-23)** Ôťů ÔÇö `compute_beam_deflection(BeamSpec) -> BeamDeflectionReport` implements six closed-form Euler-Bernoulli beam cases: (1) simply_supported + point_center: ╬┤=PL┬│/(48EI), M=PL/4 [Roark Table 8.1 case 7; AISC 3-23 diag 1]; (2) simply_supported + udl: ╬┤=5wLÔü┤/(384EI), M=wL┬▓/8 [case 2; diag 2]; (3) cantilever + point_center (tip load): ╬┤=PL┬│/(3EI), M=PL [case 1; diag 6]; (4) cantilever + udl: ╬┤=wLÔü┤/(8EI), M=wL┬▓/2 [case 3; diag 7]; (5) fixed_fixed + udl: ╬┤=wLÔü┤/(384EI), M=wL┬▓/12 [case 15; diag 9]; (6) fixed_fixed + point_center Ôťů: ╬┤=PL┬│/(192EI), M_support=PL/8 (hogging, governs), M_center=PL/8 (sagging), ╬┤(x)=Px┬▓(3LÔłĺ4x)/(48EI) for 0ÔëĄxÔëĄL/2 [Roark Table 8.1 case 8; AISC 3-23 diag 8]. `BeamDeflectionReport` returns ╬┤_max_mm, M_max_Nmm, V_max_N, deflection_location_mm, honest_caveat. `arch_compute_beam_deflection` LLM tool registered in plugin; gated import (registry unavailable Ôćĺ module still importable). **ARCH-OPENING-IN-WALL (IBC ┬ž2308.4 + ACI 318-19 ┬ž11.5.3.1 + TMS 402-22 ┬ž5/┬ž8.3)** Ôťů ÔÇö `check_opening(WallOpeningSpec) -> OpeningCheckReport` checks a wall opening (door/window) for code-compliant tributary load redistribution to jamb piers and lintel/header adequacy. Oracle (concrete, 3m wall, 200mm thick, 1.2m├Ś1.5m window, fc=30MPa, jamb=0.4m, axial=30kN/m, lateral=1.0kN/m┬▓): trib_w=1.8m, Pu=65.7kN, ¤ć┬ĚPnÔëł812kN, jamb DCRÔëł0.081; all_adequate=True. `OpeningCheckReport` returns tributary_load_on_jamb_kN, jamb_axial_capacity_kN, jamb_dcr, lintel_moment_dcr, lintel_deflection_mm, all_adequate, governing_check, honest_caveat. `arch_check_opening_in_wall` LLM tool registered in plugin (gated import); re-exported from arch/__init__.py. 25 hermetic oracle tests pass ÔÇö `packages/kerf-cad-core/src/kerf_cad_core/arch/opening_in_wall.py`. *SCOPE: SIMPLIFIED TRIBUTARY METHOD ÔÇö full 2-D FE stress-concentration analysis around opening corners NOT modelled (St. Venant diffusion Ôëł 1ÔÇô2├Ś opening dimension; may be unconservative for wide openings > wall_height/2 or clustered openings). **ARCH-PIER-AXIAL (TMS 402-22 ┬ž8.3 + ACI 318-19 ┬ž22.4.2.2 + Drysdale-Hamid ┬ž10)** Ôťů ÔÇö `check_pier_axial(PierSpec, P_factored_kN, phi=0.65) -> PierAxialReport` implements axial-load capacity of slender masonry and reinforced concrete piers with TMS Eq 8-22 h/r slenderness reduction. **ARCH-RETAINING-WALL-STABILITY (Bowles 5e ┬ž12.3 + Das ┬ž13 ÔÇö Rankine active)** Ôťů ÔÇö `check_retaining_wall(RetainingWallSpec, SoilSpec) -> RetainingWallReport` implements overturning, sliding, and bearing stability checks for cantilevered concrete retaining walls under Rankine active earth pressure. Bearing: e = B/2 Ôłĺ (M_resistÔłĺM_overt)/╬úW; q_max = (╬úW/B)┬Ě(1+6e/B) (trapezoidal; triangular when e>B/6); FoS_bearing = q_a/q_max (min 3.0). `RetainingWallReport` returns Ka, Pa_kN_per_m, FoS_overturning, FoS_sliding, q_max_kPa, FoS_bearing, all_adequate, governing_failure_mode, honest_caveat. **ARCH-LATERAL-BRACING (AISC 360-22 ┬žF2 + AISC Manual Table 3-2)** Ôťů ÔÇö `check_lateral_bracing(WSectionSpec, L_b_mm, Cb=1.0) -> LateralBracingReport` implements AISC 360-22 ┬žF2 LRFD for compact doubly symmetric I-shaped members bent about the major axis. **GDT-DATUM-PRECEDENCE-WARN (ASME Y14.5-2018 ┬ž4.7 + ┬ž4.11)** Ôťů ÔÇö `analyze_datum_precedence_consistency(frames, datums) -> PrecedenceReport` checks a set of feature control frames for cross-frame datum inconsistencies: P1 feature-type conflict (same datum letter as planar in one frame, FOS in another ÔÇö ERROR); P1b datum at multiple precedence levels ÔÇö WARNING; P2 precedence reversal (A|B|C vs B|A|C ÔÇö WARNING, ┬ž4.11); P3 DOF over-constraint (>6 DOF from declared datum sequence ÔÇö ERROR, ┬ž4.7); P4 modifier conflict (RMB vs MMB vs LMB on same datum ÔÇö WARNING, ┬ž4.11.5). `PrecedenceReport` dataclass: `warnings`, `consistent`, `frames_analysed`, `recommendations`. Each `PrecedenceWarning`: `code`, `severity` (ERROR/WARNING), `message`, `rule`, `affected_frames`, `datum_label`, `recommendation`. `gdt_warn_datum_precedence` LLM tool registered. DOF budget per ┬ž4.7: planar primary=3, cylinder primary=2, sphere primary=3, planar secondary=2, FOS secondary=1, tertiary=1. HONEST FLAG: analyses declared datum properties only ÔÇö geometric consistency requires the solid model. Oracles: Fig. 4-1 (3-2-1 planar Ôćĺ clean); Fig. 4-2 (FOS cylinder primary RMB Ôćĺ clean); ┬ž4.11 text (A|B|C vs B|A|C Ôćĺ PRECEDENCE_REVERSAL). 41 tests ÔÇö `packages/kerf-gdnt/src/kerf_gdnt/datum_precedence_warn.py`.

### Latest delta ÔÇö 2026-05-30

Degenerate-ray honest flag: if primary direction is parallel to a face, fallback direction (0.017, 1, 0.011) is tried; if both disagree on parity, `degenerate_ray=True` and `inside=None`. LLM tool `brep_solid_contains_point` registered. Re-exported from `geom/__init__.py`. **NURBS-CURVE-FRESNEL-PARAMETERIZE** Ôťů ÔÇö `fresnel_parameterize_curve(curve, num_samples=200, target_kappa_rate=1.0)` returns `FresnelParameterizationResult(curve_out, max_curvature_residual, fresnel_S, fresnel_C, honest_caveat)`; re-parameterizes a NurbsCurve so that curvature grows linearly with arc-length (╬║(s) Ôëł ╬▒┬Ěs ÔÇö Euler spiral / clothoid / Cornu spiral law). Algorithm: (1) arc-lengthÔÇôuniform sampling via adaptive 5-pt Gauss-Legendre; (2) Fresnel integral evaluation C(¤â), S(¤â) with ¤â=s┬ĚÔłÜ(╬▒/¤Ç) (Abramowitz-Stegun ┬ž7.3); (3) monotone Fresnel-C parameter sequence drives NURBS re-interpolation (Piegl-Tiller ┬ž9.2); (4) monotone-blend fallback when spiral winds past first inflection. Degree-1 polyline caveat; zero-length degenerate guard; negative-alpha treated as positive. LLM tool `nurbs_fresnel_parameterize_curve` registered (gated import). Re-exported from `geom/__init__.py`. 25 hermetic tests. HONEST: sampling-based, not closed-form; Fresnel monotone blend active for long curves; curvature residual is approximate. Refs: Walton & Meek (2009) ┬ž┬ž2ÔÇô3; Bertolazzi & Frego (2015) ┬ž3 ÔÇö `kerf-cad-core/geom/fresnel_parameterize.py`.

**NURBS-CURVE-INFLECTION** Ôťů ÔÇö v2 API: `find_curve_inflections(curve, num_samples=200, tol=1e-6)` returns `CurveInflectionReport(inflection_points, num_inflections, max_curvature, min_curvature, is_fair_class_a, warnings, honest_caveat)`; each inflection is an `InflectionPoint(parameter_u, xy_mm, curvature_left, curvature_right, sign_change)`. Signed curvature ╬║(u) = (x'┬Ěy'' Ôłĺ y'┬Ěx'') / (x'┬▓ + y'┬▓)^1.5 (Piegl-Tiller ┬ž5.3; Farin ┬ž10.6). Algorithm: sample ╬║(u) at `num_samples` uniform u-values via NURBS 1st/2nd derivatives Ôćĺ adjacent sign-change detection (|╬║| < tol treated as zero) Ôćĺ 5-iteration bisection per bracket Ôćĺ `is_fair_class_a = True` iff ÔëĄ 1 inflection AND no abrupt ╬║-jump (>5├Ś mean, Farin ┬ž10.6; Sapidis ┬ž3). Legacy v1 API (`find_curve_inflections_v1` Ôćĺ `InflectionResult`) retained for backward compat. LLM tool `nurbs_find_curve_inflections` updated to return v2 payload. Re-exported from `geom/__init__.py`. 38 hermetic tests (20 legacy + 18 new; oracles: S-curve Ôćĺ 1 inflection + fair, double-S sine Ôćĺ Ôëą2 + not fair, circle Ôćĺ 0 + fair + ╬║Ôëł1/R, straight line Ôćĺ 0 + fair + warns). HONEST: **2D only** ÔÇö 3D space-curve inflections (requiring torsion) not supported; sampling-based, does NOT solve ╬║=0 analytically; near-zero-curvature regions may produce false positives or miss gentle crossings. Refs: Piegl-Tiller ┬ž5.3/┬ž9.2; Farin ┬ž10.6; do Carmo ┬ž1.5; Sapidis ┬ž3 ÔÇö `kerf-cad-core/geom/curve_inflection.py`. **NURBS-CURVE-INFLECTION-STURM** Ôťů (analytic Sturm inflection now implemented) ÔÇö v3 API: `find_curve_inflections_sturm(curve, tol=1e-9)` adds a true analytic root finder via Sturm sequences (Marden ┬ž1.4; Uspensky ┬ž5) on the polynomial numerator p(t) = x'(t)┬Ěy''(t) Ôłĺ y'(t)┬Ěx''(t). Algorithm: (1) decompose non-rational B-spline into Bezier segments; (2) convert Bernstein CPs to monomial basis (Farin ┬ž5.1; Farouki-Rajan 1987); (3) form p(s) of degree 2dÔłĺ3 per span; (4) build Sturm chain {p_0=p, p_1=p', p_{k+1}=Ôłĺrem(p_{k-1},p_k)}; (5) count roots via V(0)ÔłĺV(1); (6) isolate each root by recursive Sturm-bisection to tol. Returns same `CurveInflectionReport` with `honest_caveat` noting `method='sturm-analytic'`. Rational NURBS fall back with warning (numerator is rational, not polynomial). 7 hermetic Sturm tests green (S-curve Ôćĺ 1 root near midpoint, double-S Ôćĺ Ôëą2, Sturm vs v2 agreement, straight line Ôćĺ 0, circle rational Ôćĺ 0, honest_caveat content, asymmetric cubic accuracy). Refs: Marden (1966) ┬ž1.4; Uspensky (1948) ┬ž5; Farin (2002) ┬ž5.1; Farouki-Rajan (1987) CAGD 4(4).

**NURBS-CURVE-EVOLUTE** Ôťů ÔÇö `compute_curve_evolute(curve, num_samples=200, min_curvature=1e-6)` returns `EvoluteResult(evolute_points, t_params, num_samples, num_cusps_detected, cusp_t_params, honest_caveat)`; computes the locus of centres of osculating circles E(t) = C(t) + n╠é(t)/╬║(t) where n╠é is the left-hand unit normal and ╬║ is the signed curvature. Algorithm: sample t Ôłł [t_min, t_max] at `num_samples` uniform points; evaluate ╬║(t) via standard plane-curve formula ╬║ = (x'y'' Ôłĺ y'x'')/(x'┬▓+y'┬▓)^(3/2) using NURBS analytical derivatives; skip samples where |╬║| < min_curvature (evolute diverges); detect cusps (vertices of C) as local extrema of |╬║| via windowed comparison with amplitude guard (suppresses floating-point chatter on constant-╬║ curves). Circle oracle: all evolute points within 1.6e-15 of center. Parabola y=x┬▓/2: apex evolute = (0,1) exactly. Ellipse a=2,b=1: 4 cusps (stretched-astroid evolute). Straight line: evolute empty. LLM tool `nurbs_compute_curve_evolute` registered (gated import). Re-exported from `geom/__init__.py`. 20 hermetic tests. HONEST: **2D curves only** ÔÇö 3D Frenet-Serret evolutes (requiring torsion) are not yet supported; cusp detection is windowed/amplitude-gated and depends on sample density; may miss cusps for highly undersampled curves. Applications: cycloidal-gear design, cam-profile cusp analysis, CNC offset self-intersection prediction. Refs: do Carmo ┬ž1.6; Mortenson ┬ž4.2 ÔÇö `kerf-cad-core/geom/curve_evolute.py`.

**NURBS-SURFACE-CROSS-SECTION** Ôťů ÔÇö `compute_surface_cross_section(surface, plane_point, plane_normal, nu=50, nv=50)` returns `SurfaceCrossSectionResult(intersection_points_3d, num_intersections, num_components, is_closed_loop, honest_caveat)`; computes the planar cross-section curve C(t) of a NurbsSurface S(u,v) intersected with a plane P (point + normal). Algorithm (Sederberg CAGD ┬ž7.3; Patrikalakis-Maekawa ┬ž5): (1) sample S(u,v) on a (nu ├Ś nv) uniform grid over the knot domain; (2) compute signed distance d(u,v) = (S Ôłĺ P) ┬Ě n╠é for each sample; (3) walk all u-direction and v-direction grid edges, detect sign changes (d_A * d_B < 0); (4) refine each crossing via 5 bisection iterations in (u,v) parameter space (positional error Ôëł cell_size/32); (5) chain intersection points into polyline components via greedy nearest-neighbour walk; (6) detect closed loops (first Ôëł last point within 3├Ś mean spacing). Oracles: sphere R=2 Ôłę XY plane (mean radius within 20%), cylinder Ôłę XZ plane (2 components, yÔëł0), flat patch Ôłę parallel plane (empty), torus Ôłę z=0 (inner/outer rings), non-unit normal idempotent, zero normal safe. LLM tool `nurbs_compute_surface_cross_section` registered via gated import. Re-exported from `geom/__init__.py`. 22 hermetic tests green. HONEST: **sample-based** ÔÇö sub-cell features (thin necks, tangential near-grazing crossings) may be missed at low nu/nv; 5-iteration bisection (not sub-pixel for coarse grids); component ordering greedy nearest-neighbour (may mis-order interleaved loops); closed-loop detection threshold-based. Refs: Sederberg CAGD ┬ž7.3; Patrikalakis-Maekawa ┬ž5 ÔÇö `kerf-cad-core/geom/surface_cross_section.py`.

**NURBS uniform arc-length resample** Ôťů ÔÇö `resample_uniform_arc_length(curve, samples=100)` returns `ResampleResult(points, parameters, arc_lengths, total_length, fitted_curve, degenerate)`; arc-length inversion via bisection on adaptive 5-pt Gauss-Legendre integral (Piegl-Tiller ┬ž9.4 + Patrikalakis-Maekawa ┬ž3.5); `fit=True` returns interpolated NurbsCurve; degenerate flag for zero-length curves; LLM tool `nurbs_curve_resample_uniform`; 12 analytic-oracle tests (circle 2¤Ç/100 ┬▒ 0.001, parabola arc-uniform < param-uniform variance, line sqrt(2)/10 ┬▒ 1e-6, degenerate flag). Honest: GL quadrature ~1e-9 accurate; highly-oscillatory curves may need larger `max_depth`.

Four MFR bands (low < 5, medium 5ÔÇô25, high 25ÔÇô100, super-high > 100 g/10 min); wall-thickness and gate-type correction factors applied; qualitative risk flags for gate freeze, jetting, and sink marks. **MOLD-COOLING-TURBULENT-RE-CHECK** Ôťů ÔÇö `check_turbulent_re(CoolingFlowSpec) -> TurbulentReCheckReport` in `kerf_mold.cooling_turbulent_re_check`. Verifies cooling-channel Reynolds number Re = ¤ü┬Ěv┬ĚD/╬╝ against the fully-turbulent threshold (Re Ôëą 10 000) required for Dittus-Boelter correlation validity (Incropera & DeWitt eq. 8.60: Nu=0.023┬ĚRe^0.8┬ĚPr^n). Flow-regime classification (White "Fluid Mechanics" ┬ž8.1): Re<2300 Ôćĺ "laminar" (AVOID ÔÇö thermally stratified, very poor cooling), 2300ÔëĄRe<4000 Ôćĺ "transitional" (unpredictable; avoid), 4000ÔëĄRe<10000 Ôćĺ "turbulent" (Dittus-Boelter valid but h sub-optimal), ReÔëą10000 Ôćĺ "fully_turbulent" (target for mold cooling, Beaumont 2007 ┬ž11). Also computes minimum recommended flow rate [L/min] to reach Re=10000 for the given channel geometry and coolant. Dataclasses: `CoolingFlowSpec` (channel_diameter_mm, flow_rate_L_per_min, coolant_density_kg_m3=1000, coolant_viscosity_cP=1.0); `TurbulentReCheckReport` (reynolds_number, flow_regime, velocity_m_per_s, recommended_min_flow_rate_L_per_min, dittus_boelter_applicable, honest_caveat). Unit conversions: mmÔćĺm, L/minÔćĺm┬│/s├Ě60000, cPÔćĺPa┬Ěs. LLM tool `mold_check_turbulent_re` registered in plugin.py; re-exported from `kerf_mold/__init__.py`. 24 tests green. **HONEST SCOPE: Re classification ONLY** ÔÇö does NOT compute Nusselt number / convective HTC (requires Prandtl number input), polymer-side boundary layer, mold-steel wall thermal resistance, or part-steel contact resistance; does NOT model wall heat flux or non-uniform temperature distribution along the channel; single-phase, isothermal, incompressible, Newtonian fluid only (no two-phase/supercritical COÔéé cooling); viscosity spatially uniform (re-run with exit viscosity for ╬öT > 10 ┬░C); circular cross-section assumed (non-circular channels: supply hydraulic diameter D_h=4A/P) ÔÇö `packages/kerf-mold/src/kerf_mold/cooling_turbulent_re_check.py`. Refs: Beaumont 2007 ┬ž11 (cooling-system Re requirement); White "Fluid Mechanics" 8th ed. ┬ž8.1 (Re thresholds); Incropera & DeWitt "Heat and Mass Transfer" 7th ed. ┬ž8.5 eq. 8.60 (Dittus-Boelter ReÔëą10000).

**MOLD-CORE-PIN-COOLING** Ôťů ÔÇö `design_core_pin_cooling(CorePinSpec) -> CorePinCoolingReport` in `kerf_mold.core_pin_cooling`. Interior baffle/bubbler cooling design for slender injection-mold core pins (tall rib inserts). Re = 4┬ĚQ┬Ě¤ü/(¤Ç┬ĚD_h┬Ě╬╝) (volumetric form); Nusselt number Nu = 0.023┬ĚRe^0.8┬ĚPr^0.4 (Dittus-Boelter, Incropera eq. 8.60); HTC h = Nu┬Ěk_f/D_h; bubbler mode applies a 2├Ś HTC multiplier relative to baffle per Menges 2001 ┬ž7.5 and Beaumont 2007 ┬ž11.4 (fountain-effect tip cooling + annular return turbulence). Core-tip temperature from 1-D lumped steady-state resistance network: R_poly = 1/(h_p┬ĚA_surface) (h_p = 2000 W/m┬▓K, Menges ┬ž7.1 midpoint); R_steel = L_half/(k_steel┬ĚA_cross) (k_steel = 15 W/m┬ĚK P20/H13); R_cool = 1/(h┬ĚA_bore). Cycle-time estimate by Menges 2001 ┬ž7.3.3 / Chen-Chiang 1985 first-term Fourier: t_c = (h_wall┬▓/¤Ç┬▓╬▒)┬Ěln[(8/¤Ç┬▓)┬Ě(T_meltÔłĺT_cool)/(T_ejectÔłĺT_cool)]; ╬▒ = 1.0e-7 m┬▓/s (ABS baseline). Oracle (30 mm core, 100 mm tall, baffle, 4 mm ID, 2 L/min water at 20 ┬░C, Pr=7): Re = 10610, Nu = 83.2, HTC = 12445 W/m┬▓K; bubbler HTC = 24890 W/m┬▓K (2.000├Ś ratio); cycle-time = 248 s. `cooling_adequate = True` iff Re Ôëą 10 000 AND T_tip ÔëĄ target. `CorePinSpec` dataclass (core_diameter_mm, core_height_mm, baffle_or_bubbler: "baffle"|"bubbler", cooling_type_id_mm, coolant_flow_L_per_min, melt_temp_C, target_core_temp_C, polymer_grade, coolant_temp_C=20, density, viscosity, Pr, k_f); `CorePinCoolingReport` dataclass (reynolds_number, htc_W_per_m2K, estimated_core_tip_temp_C, cooling_adequate, cycle_time_estimate_s, honest_caveat). Refs: Menges G., Michaeli W., Mohren P. "How to Make Injection Molds" 3rd ed. Hanser 2001 ┬ž7.5 (core-pin cooling) + ┬ž7.1 (polymer HTC) + ┬ž7.3.3 (cooling-time formula); Beaumont J.P. **MOLD-EJECTOR-PIN-PUSH** Ôťů ÔÇö `compute_ejector_pin_push(EjectorPinPushSpec) -> EjectorPinPushReport` in `kerf_mold.ejector_pin_push`. Computes the Euler critical buckling load for an SPI/ANSI B151.1 ejector pin and verifies it against the required push force. Formula: F_cr = ¤Ç┬▓┬ĚE┬ĚI/(K┬ĚL)┬▓  (Roark's 9e ┬ž15.2); I = ¤Ç┬ĚdÔü┤/64 (solid round section); E = 200 GPa for all tool-steel grades (M2_tool_steel, H13, S7, D2 ÔÇö all share the same nominal Young's modulus). End-condition coefficient K: 1.0 pinned-pinned (SPI/ANSI B151.1 default for guided pins), 0.5 fixed-fixed, 0.7 fixed-pinned, 2.0 cantilever. Dataclasses: `EjectorPinPushSpec` (pin_diameter_mm, pin_length_L_mm, pin_material: "M2_tool_steel"|"H13"|"S7"|"D2", end_condition_K=1.0, required_push_force_N); `EjectorPinPushReport` (buckling_force_N, dcr=required/F_cr, adequate: bool, recommended_min_diameter_mm, recommended_pin_material, honest_caveat). Recommendation logic: searches SPI standard diameters (1, 1.5, 2, 2.5, 3, 4, 5, 6, 8, 10, 12, 16, 20 mm) for the smallest diameter with F_cr Ôëą 1.1 ├Ś required_push_force_N at the same L and K; prefers M2 when DCR > 0.8. Numeric oracle: 8 mm, L=100 mm, K=1: F_cr = ¤Ç┬│┬Ě200000┬Ě64/10000 Ôëł 39 688 N; 4 mm pin is 16├Ś weaker than 8 mm (I ÔłŁ dÔü┤); doubling L reduces F_cr by 4├Ś. LLM tool `mold_compute_ejector_pin_push` registered in plugin.py; re-exported from `kerf_mold/__init__.py`. 45 oracle tests green. **HONEST SCOPE: Euler formula only** ÔÇö non-conservative for short/stout pins (K┬ĚL/d < 30); use Johnson parabolic formula F_cr_J = A┬Ě¤â_y┬Ě[1 Ôłĺ ¤â_y┬Ě(K┬ĚL/r)┬▓/(4┬Ě¤Ç┬▓┬ĚE)] in that regime (function flags the warning in honest_caveat); bushing friction (╬╝Ôëł0.05ÔÇô0.10 lubricated, reduces capacity 3ÔÇô10 %) and pin eccentricity/TIR beam-column amplification (Roark's 9e ┬ž15.3) are NOT modelled; dynamic ejection impact and fatigue over millions of cycles are NOT assessed; confirm by mold-trial load-cell measurement ÔÇö `packages/kerf-mold/src/kerf_mold/ejector_pin_push.py`. Refs: SPI/ANSI B151.1; Roark R.J. & Young W.C. Formulas for Stress and Strain, 9th ed., ┬ž15.2ÔÇô15.3; ASM Handbook Vol.1 (tool-steel E values).

**MOLD-TUNNEL-GATE-DESIGN** Ôťů ÔÇö `design_tunnel_gate(TunnelGateSpec) -> TunnelGateReport` in `kerf_mold.tunnel_gate_design`. Designs a tunnel (submarine) gate given part weight and polymer grade. Diameter: D = 0.5 ├Ś wall_thickness (Beaumont 2007 ┬ž7.4); +10 % high-viscosity correction for PC/PA66/PMMA/POM/PEI/PPO; lower bound 0.8 mm (machining floor); upper cap D ÔëĄ 2/3 ├Ś wall_thickness (Menges 2001 ┬ž6.6.5). Break-off force: F = ¤ä_shear ├Ś ¤Ç/4┬ĚD┬▓ using Menges 2001 Table 6.3 shear strengths (ABS=30, PC=45, PP=22, PA66=40, POM=38, PMMA=42, PEI=50, PPO=45 MPa). Shear rate: ╬│╠ç = 4Q/(¤Ç┬Ěr┬│) (Hagen-Poiseuille, Newtonian); Q = (m_part/¤ü_melt) / 1.0 s; Beaumont ┬ž7.4 limit 50 000 sÔü╗┬╣; `shear_within_limit` flag. Gate freeze time: t_f = (D┬▓/¤Ç┬▓┬Ě╬▒)┬Ěln[(8/¤Ç┬▓)┬Ě(T_meltÔłĺT_mold)/(T_ejectÔłĺT_mold)] per Chen-Chiang ANTEC 1985 / Menges 2001 ┬ž7.3.3. Angle recommendation: 30┬░ for flexible/low-viscosity, 45┬░ for stiff/high-viscosity (Menges ┬ž6.6.5). Oracle: ABS, 30 g, wall 2 mm Ôćĺ D = 1.0 mm; F_break = 23.6 N; freeze time Ôëł 1.42 s. `TunnelGateSpec` (part_weight_g, wall_thickness_at_gate_mm, polymer_grade, melt_temp_C, gate_angle_deg=30.0, gate_length_mm=1.5); `TunnelGateReport` (gate_diameter_mm, gate_break_off_force_N, gate_freeze_time_s, shear_rate_at_gate_per_s, shear_within_limit, recommended_angle_deg, honest_caveat). LLM tool `mold_design_tunnel_gate` registered in plugin.py; re-exported from `kerf_mold/__init__.py`. 35 tests green. **HONEST: Beaumont heuristic ÔÇö diameter is a start-point only; complex multi-cavity timing and fill-pressure balance require Moldflow/Moldex3D full 3-D fill simulation; break-off force sensitive to mold temperature and specific resin grade ductility; shear rate is Newtonian approximation (actual shear-thinning ╬│╠ç Ôëł 1.25ÔÇô1.5├Ś higher); freeze time is 1-D Fourier constant-diffusivity (PP/PA66/POM actual 15ÔÇô25 % longer due to crystallisation latent heat); confirm by mold trial** ÔÇö `packages/kerf-mold/src/kerf_mold/tunnel_gate_design.py`. Refs: Beaumont J.P. "Runner and Gating Design Handbook" 2nd ed. Hanser 2007 ┬ž7.4; Menges G., Michaeli W., Mohren P. "How to Make Injection Molds" 3rd ed. Hanser 2001 ┬ž6.6.5 + Table 6.3 + ┬ž7.3.3; Chen-Chiang ANTEC 1985.

**MOLD-SURFACE-FINISH-CHECK** Ôťů ÔÇö `check_surface_finish(SurfaceFinishSpec, MoldSpec) -> SurfaceFinishReport` in `kerf_mold.surface_finish_check`. Validates that a molded part's resin + mold-steel + hardness combination can achieve the requested SPI Mold Finish Standard grade (A1ÔÇôD3), and recommends mold steel grade, minimum HRC, and polishing method. SPI grades (2017 standard): A1 Ra ÔëĄ 0.012 ┬Ám (diamond paste #3, S136 Ôëą50 HRC), A2 Ra ÔëĄ 0.025 ┬Ám (diamond buff #6, S136 Ôëą48 HRC), A3 Ra ÔëĄ 0.050 ┬Ám (diamond buff #15, S136/H13 Ôëą44 HRC); B1 Ra ÔëĄ 0.10 ┬Ám (600-grit stone, H13 Ôëą38 HRC), B2ÔÇôB3 Ra 0.20ÔÇô0.40 ┬Ám (stone, P20); C1ÔÇôC3 Ra 0.80ÔÇô3.20 ┬Ám (emery cloth, P20); D1ÔÇôD3 Ra 3.2ÔÇô14 ┬Ám (dry blast, P20). Glass-fiber rule (Menges ┬ž11.4.2): glass-reinforced resins cannot achieve A-grade on the molded part regardless of mold polish (fiber pull-out + print-through). Resin limits: PA66 Ôćĺ max A3 (crystalline skin haze); PP Ôćĺ max B1; POM Ôćĺ max B2; LDPE Ôćĺ max C1. Steel limits: S136 Ôćĺ A1; 420SS Ôćĺ A2; H13 Ôćĺ A3; P20 Ôćĺ B3. Dataclasses: `SurfaceFinishSpec` (required_finish, resin); `MoldSpec` (mold_steel, hardness_HRC, mold_finish_achieved=""); `SurfaceFinishReport` (achievable, recommended_steel, recommended_hardness_HRC_min, recommended_polishing_method, Ra_target_um, Ra_achievable_um, glass_filled_warning, honest_caveat). LLM tool `mold_check_surface_finish` registered in plugin.py; re-exported from `kerf_mold/__init__.py`. 27 tests green. **HONEST: catalog-based checker ÔÇö does NOT model texture chemistry (etching achievability depends on etch bath + resin crystallinity), etcher capability (bath concentration + cycle count not modelled), polishing wear-life (abrasive filler content + shot count not modelled), part-geometry effects (weld lines + deep ribs harder to polish), or process variables (mold temperature, hold pressure, cooling time affect surface replication fidelity)** ÔÇö `packages/kerf-mold/src/kerf_mold/surface_finish_check.py`. Refs: SPI/PLASTICS Mold Finish Standards 2017; Menges G., Mohren P. "How to Make Injection Molds" 3rd ed. Hanser 2001 ┬ž11; Bryce D. M. "Plastic Injection Molding: Mold Design and Construction Fundamentals" SME 1998 Ch. 8.

**MOLD-COLOR-CONCENTRATE-RATIO** Ôťů ÔÇö `compute_color_ratio(ColorConcentrateSpec, ShotSpec) -> ColorRatioReport` in `kerf_mold.color_concentrate_ratio`. Gravimetric let-down ratio (LDR) dosing and mixing-quality assessment for color concentrate (masterbatch) in injection moulding. LDR formula (SPI Color Concentrates Handbook 3rd ed. ┬ž3): LDR (%) = target_pigment_loading_pct / pigment_loading_in_masterbatch_pct ├Ś 100. Masterbatch per shot [g] = shot_weight_g ├Ś LDR/100; masterbatch per kg natural resin [g/kg] = 1000 ├Ś (LDR/100) / (1 Ôłĺ LDR/100). SPI recommended LDR range: 1ÔÇô5 %. Mixing index heuristic (Menges Plastics Manufacturing ┬ž10.2; Tadmor & Gogos ┬ž12.5): mixing_index = 1 Ôłĺ exp(Ôłĺbarrel_residence_s ├Ś screw_L/D / 200); adequate if > 0.80. Streaking-risk classification: low (LDR 1ÔÇô5 % AND mixing_index > 0.80), moderate (marginal LDR 0.5ÔÇô1 % or 5ÔÇô8 %, or mixing_index ÔëĄ 0.80 with LDR in range), high (LDR < 0.5 % ÔÇö too dilute for shot-to-shot uniformity ÔÇö or LDR > 8 % ÔÇö cost-waste territory / mechanical-property dilution risk per Menges ┬ž10.4). Dataclasses: `ColorConcentrateSpec` (pigment_loading_in_masterbatch_pct, recommended_let_down_pct, carrier_resin, melting_temp_C); `ShotSpec` (shot_weight_g, target_pigment_loading_pct, barrel_residence_time_s, screw_L_over_D=20.0); `ColorRatioReport` (let_down_ratio_pct, masterbatch_per_shot_g, masterbatch_per_kg_natural, mixing_index_estimate, color_streaking_risk, warnings, honest_caveat). Oracle: 100 g shot, target 1 % pigment, MB at 40 % Ôćĺ LDR = 2.5 %, MB = 2.5 g/shot, MB per kg natural Ôëł 25.64 g/kg. LLM tool `mold_compute_color_concentrate_ratio` registered in plugin.py; re-exported from `kerf_mold/__init__.py`. 40 tests green. **HONEST: mixing index is a heuristic exponential-decay proxy from L/D and residence time only ÔÇö does NOT model screw-flight geometry, back-pressure, screw speed, melt-viscosity mismatch between masterbatch carrier and natural resin, pellet size ratio, or colorant particle agglomerate size; LDR is gravimetric only (volumetric accuracy requires density-matched MB and natural resin); streaking-risk classification is a screening guideline ÔÇö trial colour plaques with L*a*b* colorimetric measurement per ISO 11664-4 are the only reliable acceptance test; carrier resin compatibility must be confirmed against base resin; empirical mixing estimate, NOT a substitute for colour-master trial shots** ÔÇö `packages/kerf-mold/src/kerf_mold/color_concentrate_ratio.py`. Refs: SPI "Color Concentrates Handbook" 3rd ed. ┬ž3, ┬ž6, ┬ž8, ┬ž11; Menges G., Kemper B., Klenk E. "Plastics Manufacturing" ┬ž10; Tadmor Z. & Gogos C. "Principles of Polymer Processing" 2nd ed. Wiley 2006, ┬ž12.5.

**Manufacturing depth** Ôťů ÔÇö **MOLD-EJECTOR-STROKE-VERIFY** (Beaumont 2007 ┬ž9 + Menges 2001 ┬ž7.4): `verify_ejector_stroke()` ÔÇö (1) stroke adequacy: required_stroke (part_depth + safety_margin) ÔëĄ machine_stroke; (2) force capacity: pin_count ├Ś max_force Ôëą ejection_force (Menges ┬ž7.4); (3) pin deflection: ╬┤=F┬ĚL┬│/(3┬ĚE┬ĚI) ÔëĄ 0.05mm allowable (Euler-Bernoulli cantilever, Beaumont ┬ž9.3, I=¤Ç┬ĚdÔü┤/64, E=200 GPa steel); (4) knockout bar contact: plate_thickness Ôëą bar_diameter (Beaumont ┬ž9.5); `EjectorStrokeReport` dataclass (stroke_adequate, force_per_pin, max_deflection_mm, violations); LLM tool `mold_verify_ejector_stroke` registered; 33 oracle tests; static load only (honest-flagged: no dynamic ejection force, shrinkage grip, thermal expansion, or pin fatigue) ÔÇö `packages/kerf-mold/src/kerf_mold/ejector_stroke_verify.py` Ôťů.
**Manufacturing depth** Ôťů ÔÇö **MOLD-WALL-THICKNESS-FLOW-LEAD** (Beaumont 2007 ┬ž4 Table 4.2 + Menges 2001 ┬ž6.2.1): `compute_flow_length_check()` ÔÇö flow-length-to-wall-thickness (L/T) ratio per cavity feature; primary short-shot risk indicator; MATERIAL_LT_LIMITS dict (ABS=150, PC=220, PP=300, PA66=250, POM=200, PMMA=180); risk: ÔëĄ80% limit Ôćĺ safe, 80ÔÇô100% Ôćĺ caution, >100% Ôćĺ short_shot; recommended_min_thickness_mm = flow_length/(limit├Ś0.85) (15% safety margin); `FlowFeature` + `FlowLengthReport` dataclasses; LLM tool `mold_check_flow_length` registered; 23 oracle tests; honest-flagged: L/T ratio only ÔÇö NOT Hagen-Poiseuille pressure-drop simulation, melt-front thermal analysis, or multi-gate flow balance; use Moldflow/Moldex3D/SigmaSoft for full fill simulation ÔÇö `packages/kerf-mold/src/kerf_mold/flow_length_check.py` Ôťů.
**Manufacturing depth** Ôťů ÔÇö **MOLD-COOLING-TIME-CHEN-CHIANG** (Chen-Chiang 1985 + Menges 2001 ┬ž7.3.3 + Beaumont 2007 ┬ž10.4): `compute_cooling_time_chen_chiang()` ÔÇö 1-D Fourier first-term cooling-time formula: t_c = (h┬▓/¤Ç┬▓╬▒)┬Ěln[(8/¤Ç┬▓)┬Ě(T_mÔłĺT_w)/(T_eÔłĺT_w)]; `MaterialThermalProps` dataclass (name, thermal_diffusivity_m2_per_s, T_melt_C, T_ejection_C); `CoolingTimeReport` dataclass (wall_thickness_mm, cooling_time_s, dominant_factor, material_used, honest_caveat); MATERIAL_THERMAL_DB (Menges 2001 Table 7.3): ABS ╬▒=1.00e-7, PC ╬▒=1.50e-7, PP ╬▒=0.95e-7, PA66 ╬▒=1.40e-7, POM ╬▒=0.95e-7, PMMA ╬▒=1.13e-7 m┬▓/s; dominant-factor diagnosis (thickness_squared|diffusivity|temp_window) via log-sensitivity; LLM tool `mold_compute_cooling_time_chen_chiang` registered; 24 oracle tests; honest-flagged: 1-D Fourier first-term approximation only ÔÇö ignores cooling-channel layout and conformal-cooling effects; does NOT model crystallisation latent heat (semi-crystalline PP/PA66/POM times 15ÔÇô30% longer), thermal contact resistance, or hot-spot effects from varying wall thickness; use Moldflow/Moldex3D/SigmaSoft for a full cooling-circuit simulation ÔÇö `packages/kerf-mold/src/kerf_mold/cooling_time_chen_chiang.py` Ôťů.
**Manufacturing depth** Ôťů ÔÇö **MOLD-RUNNER-BALANCE-CHECK** (Beaumont 2007 ┬ž6.6 + Menges 2001 ┬ž6.6.4): `check_runner_balance()` ÔÇö Hagen-Poiseuille hydraulic resistance path check for multi-cavity runner networks; R_norm = L/rÔü┤ per segment (╬╝ cancels in ratios); path resistance summed sprueÔćĺgate via parent-pointer walk; max_imbalance_pct = 100├Ś(R_maxÔłĺR_min)/R_mean; balanced=True iff max_imbalance_pct < 5 % (Beaumont 2007 ┬ž6.6 criterion); `RunnerSegment` dataclass (id, length_mm, diameter_mm, parent_id); `RunnerBalanceReport` dataclass (cavity_paths[{cavity_id, total_length_mm, total_resistance, fill_ratio}], max_imbalance_pct, balanced, honest_caveat); LLM tool `mold_check_runner_balance` registered; 42 oracle tests; honest-flagged: geometric resistance only ÔÇö does NOT model temperature-dependent or shear-thinning viscosity, shear-heating asymmetry in graduated-diameter (artificially balanced) runners (Beaumont RPI runner), or transient filling inertia; use Moldflow/Moldex3D/SigmaSoft for full rheological fill simulation ÔÇö `packages/kerf-mold/src/kerf_mold/runner_balance_check.py` Ôťů.
**Manufacturing depth** Ôťů ÔÇö mold draft-angle validation per face: arcsin(|n╠é┬Ěpull╠é|) draft angle; SPI finish grades A1ÔÇôD3 minimum lookup (Menges 2001 ┬ž3.4 + Beaumont 2007 ┬ž4); region-aware minimums (outer 0.5┬░, inner 1.0┬░, rib 1.0┬░, boss 0.5┬░); top/bottom face pass-through; degenerate-normal flagging; LLM tool `mold_validate_draft`; 38 oracle tests; v1 honest-flag: undercut detection out of scope Ôťů.

**Manufacturing depth** Ôťů ÔÇö **MOLD-DRAFT-DEMOLD-FORCE** (Beaumont 2007 ┬ž9.3 + Menges 2001 ┬ž7.4 + Table 7.6): `compute_demold_force()` ÔÇö cavity-ejection force per F = ╬╝┬Ě¤â_h┬ĚA┬Ěcos╬▒/(cos╬▒ + ╬╝┬Ěsin╬▒); shrinkage stress ¤â_h from Menges Table 7.6 (ABS=4.0, PC=3.0, PP=5.0, PA66=3.5, POM=4.5 MPa); friction ╬╝ from SPI finish class (SPI_A1=0.15 polished ÔÇŽ SPI_D1=0.40 textured); `MoldedPartSpec` dataclass (polymer_grade, contact_area_cm2, draft_angle_deg, mold_steel_finish_class); `DemoldForceReport` dataclass (demold_force_N, contact_pressure_MPa, ejector_pin_count_required, friction_coeff_used, polymer_shrinkage_stress_MPa, honest_caveat); ejector pin count = ceil(F / single_pin_capacity_N); LLM tool `mold_compute_demold_force` registered; 28 oracle tests; honest-flagged: empirical formula only ÔÇö ignores chemical adhesion (resin stick, relevant for PC/POM on polished steel), undercut/side-action geometry, dynamic ejection force, and pin fatigue; confirm by mold-trial load-cell measurement ÔÇö `packages/kerf-mold/src/kerf_mold/demold_force_check.py` Ôťů.
**Manufacturing depth** Ôťů ÔÇö **MOLD-VENT-DEPTH-CHECK** (Beaumont 2007 ┬ž8.3 Table 8.2 + Menges 2001 ┬ž6.4 Table 6.7): `check_vent_depth()` ÔÇö verify that a mold parting-line vent depth (air-escape gap) is within the polymer-specific recommended range; too shallow Ôćĺ trapped air Ôćĺ short shot / burn marks (diesel effect); too deep Ôćĺ flash; polymer database (mm): ABS 0.025ÔÇô0.038, PC 0.013ÔÇô0.025, PP 0.025ÔÇô0.050, PA66 0.013ÔÇô0.025, POM 0.013ÔÇô0.025, PMMA 0.025ÔÇô0.038, PE 0.038ÔÇô0.075; `VentSpec` dataclass (polymer_grade, proposed_depth_mm, land_length_mm=1.5, vent_width_mm=6.0); `VentDepthReport` dataclass (recommended_depth_min_mm, recommended_depth_max_mm, compliant, depth_class, polymer_notes, honest_caveat); depth_class: "too_shallow"|"correct"|"too_deep"|"flash_risk" (>25% above max); unknown polymers receive fallback range [0.013ÔÇô0.038 mm] with caveat; LLM tool `mold_check_vent_depth` registered; 35 oracle tests; honest-flagged: empirical handbook ranges only ÔÇö actual safe vent depth depends on resin batch viscosity, melt temperature, injection speed, mold surface finish, land length, and part geometry; filled/FR/rubber-toughened grades may flash within the correct band for base resin; confirm by mold trial + visual flash inspection ÔÇö `packages/kerf-mold/src/kerf_mold/vent_depth_check.py` Ôťů.
**Manufacturing depth** Ôťů ÔÇö **MOLD-VENT-SLOT-LAYOUT** (Beaumont 2007 ┬ž8.5 Vent Slot Count and Width + Menges 2001 ┬ž6.4): `generate_vent_slot_layout()` ÔÇö propose vent slot count, width (6 mm standard), and spacing for a parting-line perimeter given cavity volume, polymer grade, and injection speed; Beaumont 0.5 %-projected-area rule: total_vent_area Ôëą 0.005 ├Ś cavity_volume_mm┬│/wall_thickness; speed scaling: vent_area_factor = max(1.0, injection_speed / 50 cm┬│/s); per-slot area = 6 mm width ├Ś depth_mid ├Ś 6 mm land length (polymer-specific depth from Beaumont Table 8.2); minimum 4 slots (one per quadrant, Beaumont ┬ž8.5; Menges ┬ž6.4); maximum slots = floor(perimeter / (6 + 10 mm steel bridge)); spacing = perimeter / n_slots; `MoldVolumeSpec` dataclass (cavity_volume_cm3, parting_line_perimeter_mm, polymer_grade, injection_speed_cm3_s); `VentSlotLayoutReport` dataclass (num_vent_slots, vent_slot_width_mm, vent_slot_spacing_mm, total_vent_width_mm, air_displacement_rate_cm3_s, adequate, honest_caveat); LLM tool `mold_generate_vent_slot_layout` registered; 47 oracle tests; honest-flagged: heuristic 0.5 %-area rule from production experience ÔÇö NOT a first-principles fluid-dynamic calculation; wall thickness assumed 3 mm for area estimation; uniform spacing only (use mold_optimize_vent_placement for last-to-fill location optimisation); vent depth handled separately by mold_check_vent_depth; confirm by fill simulation (Moldflow / Moldex3D / SigmaSoft) + mold-trial visual inspection ÔÇö `packages/kerf-mold/src/kerf_mold/vent_slot_layout.py` Ôťů.
**Manufacturing depth** Ôťů ÔÇö **MOLD-RUNNER-COLD-SLUG** (Beaumont 2007 ┬ž6.7 Cold Slug Wells + Menges 2001 ┬ž6.5): `check_cold_slug_design()` ÔÇö verify cold-slug well dimensions at runner junctions in a multi-cavity mold to trap the cold leading-edge polymer melt before it reaches the gate, preventing flow lines and weak weld lines; Beaumont rule: slug well diameter = 1.5 ├Ś runner diameter, depth = 2.0 ├Ś runner diameter, ┬▒20 % tolerance band (1.2├ŚÔÇô1.8├Ś diameter, 1.6├ŚÔÇô2.4├Ś depth); `RunnerJunctionSpec` dataclass (junction_id, runner_diameter_mm, slug_well_diameter_mm, slug_well_depth_mm, polymer_grade); `ColdSlugReport` dataclass (junction_results list, total_junctions, compliant_count, honest_caveat); per-junction result: diameter_compliant, depth_compliant, slug_well_compliant, recommended_diameter_mm, recommended_depth_mm, tolerance bounds, reason; LLM tool `mold_check_cold_slug_design` registered; 32 oracle tests; honest-flagged: geometric rule-of-thumb only ÔÇö actual cold-slug capture depends on melt temperature, injection speed, and resin freeze-off time; fast-crystallising resins (POM, PA66, LCP) and filled grades may require larger wells; confirm by mold trial + gate-area visual inspection; use Moldflow / Moldex3D / SigmaSoft for full melt-front thermal and weld-line simulation ÔÇö `packages/kerf-mold/src/kerf_mold/cold_slug_check.py` Ôťů.
